# AI研讨会：探索企业级应用与未来趋势

## 开场讨论：AI时代的学习、机遇与紧迫感

**Dave Wessinger:** And my, kind of, two major investors in Dragonair
and Hillman Friedman.

**Dave Wessinger:**
我的两大主要投资者，Dragoneer（Dragoneer投资集团：一家专注于科技领域的成长型股权投资公司）和Hellman
& Friedman（Hellman & Friedman：一家全球领先的私募股权投资公司）。

**Dave Wessinger:** Spend more time trying to get me connected with
every single person that's moving well, or better or differently in AI,
so I can learn from that.

**Dave Wessinger:**
他们花了很多时间，试图让我与每一个在AI领域做得好、更好或与众不同的人建立联系，以便我能从中学习。

**Dave Wessinger:** It's a massive learning journey, and every day could
be spent with yet another company understanding their journey.

**Dave Wessinger:**
这是一个巨大的学习过程，每天都可以花在了解另一家公司的发展历程上。

**Dave Wessinger:** And they tend to connect me with ones that have had
some reasonable success.

**Dave Wessinger:** 他们倾向于把我介绍给那些已经取得一定成功的公司。

**Dave Wessinger:** And so, I'll just speak to one that's actually, um,
connected to healthcare. This is a little more financial, but do have
some healthcare customers, and then I'll talk about a healthcare
company.

**Dave Wessinger:**
所以，我先谈一个与医疗健康相关的例子。这家公司更偏向金融领域，但确实有一些医疗客户，之后我再谈一家纯粹的医疗公司。

**Dave Wessinger:** Um, the one that I saw was…. It's a really
interesting concept, and I think as I talk about other organizations.

**Dave Wessinger:**
我看到的那家公司……它的概念非常有趣，我认为在我谈论其他组织时也是如此。

**Dave Wessinger:** I'm largely talking about solutions they deliver to
the market as the priority, but invariably, I think when we think about
what might be delivered to a market.

**Dave Wessinger:**
我主要谈论的是他们向市场提供的解决方案，但当我们思考可能向市场交付什么时，情况总是如此。

**Dave Wessinger:** In our own rights, our internal stuff, we're
consuming others' solutions. So it's the same thing, just upside down.

**Dave Wessinger:**
就我们自身而言，我们的内部系统也在使用他人的解决方案。所以这其实是同一件事，只是角度不同。

**Dave Wessinger:** And the thing that they've done well, as an
organization, they struggled to deliver AI to the market.

**Dave Wessinger:**
他们作为一个组织做得很好的一点是，他们曾努力将AI推向市场，但遇到了困难。

**Dave Wessinger:** Um, and…. I think what I recognize the challenge
with, they at least iterated, was….

**Dave Wessinger:** 我认为我认识到的挑战在于，他们至少进行了迭代……

**Dave Wessinger:** They've… they're moving really well in AI now, in
the end market. Their revenue doubled year over year.

**Dave Wessinger:**
他们现在在AI领域，在终端市场上发展得非常好。他们的收入同比增长了一倍。

**Dave Wessinger:** They acquired an AI company, accelerated some of
their work, and they basically have been building agents for the last 6
months.

**Dave Wessinger:**
他们收购了一家AI公司，加速了部分工作，并且在过去6个月里一直在构建AI智能体（AI
agents：能自主感知环境、决策并执行任务的智能程序）。

**Dave Wessinger:** And driving a ton of opportunity into the business.
And so they sell it, it's an orchestration layer for their customers.

**Dave Wessinger:**
这为业务带来了大量机会。他们销售的是一个为其客户服务的编排层（orchestration
layer：用于自动化和协调复杂系统或服务之间工作流的技术层）。

**Dave Wessinger:** They productionized it versus give their end
customers an opportunity to build their own agents.

**Dave Wessinger:**
他们将其产品化，而不是让终端客户有机会自己构建智能体。

**Dave Wessinger:** And they've done extremely well, and I think
doubling revenue in a given year is pretty incredible, actually.

**Dave Wessinger:**
他们做得非常出色，我认为在一年内实现收入翻倍确实是相当了不起的成就。

**Dave Wessinger:** In terms of an outcome. So that's really positive.
The one takeaway for me there was.

**Dave Wessinger:** 从结果来看，这非常积极。我从中得到的一个启示是。

**Dave Wessinger:** He had challenged his own team, really smart,
capable people. To move with agents and build it themselves.

**Dave Wessinger:**
他曾挑战自己的团队，那些非常聪明、有能力的人，让他们利用智能体自己构建解决方案。

**Dave Wessinger:** And he gave them a certain amount of time before he
had to go outside and acquire it, and basically they got.

**Dave Wessinger:**
他给了他们一定的时间，之后他不得不向外部寻求并收购技术，基本上他们做到了。

**Dave Wessinger:** They weren't able to get to the point where you
thought they could have, and so he had to acquire.

**Dave Wessinger:** 他们没能达到他预期的水平，所以他最终不得不进行收购。

**Dave Wessinger:** And I guess my takeaway from that is no more than.

**Dave Wessinger:** 我想我从中得到的启示无非是。

**Dave Wessinger:** If we're not taking time to sharpen the saw and
learn and grow, we're gonna be always caught up with the problems of the
day and the priorities of what's gonna pull us back.

**Dave Wessinger:**
如果我们不花时间磨砺自己、学习和成长，我们就会永远被日常问题和那些拖后腿的优先事项所困扰。

**Dave Wessinger:** And I think getting focused on where we need to go
is a lot of courage from leadership, is a lot of courage from all of us.

**Dave Wessinger:**
我认为，专注于我们需要前进的方向，需要领导层和我们所有人的巨大勇气。

**Dave Wessinger:** And I think it's not what you say yes to, it's what
you say no to.

**Dave Wessinger:**
而且我认为，关键不在于你答应了什么，而在于你拒绝了什么。

**Dave Wessinger:** And I think the one thing we hear around this
organization a lot.

**Dave Wessinger:** 我认为我们在这个组织里经常听到的一件事是。

**Dave Wessinger:** Is there's a lot of priorities, and the priorities
come down to leadership. And if we're not really clear.

**Dave Wessinger:**
有太多的优先事项，而这些优先事项最终都归结于领导层。如果我们不非常清楚。

**Dave Wessinger:** With where we need to go, what we need to choose,
we're not gonna make that progress. No matter how much learning we do
today.

**Dave Wessinger:**
我们需要去向何方，需要做出何种选择，我们就无法取得进步。无论我们今天学习了多少。

**Dave Wessinger:** We need to create space, um, and that's gonna be
hard, and it's gonna be hard to stomach sometimes, because that will
deviate from our current plans.

**Dave Wessinger:**
我们需要创造空间，这会很困难，有时甚至难以接受，因为它会偏离我们当前的计划。

**Dave Wessinger:** But, uh, that's kind of one example. I think…. The
other one is, um, and this is a little bit external, talking to some
companies that are leveraging AI to drive their growth.

**Dave Wessinger:**
但这就是一个例子。我认为……另一个例子，这稍微有点外部视角，是关于一些利用AI来驱动其在医疗健康领域增长的公司。

**Dave Wessinger:** In healthcare. And one example was, there's a
company that has built an orchestration layer.

**Dave Wessinger:**
在医疗健康领域。一个例子是，有一家公司在我们的应用程序之上构建了一个编排层。

**Dave Wessinger:** On top of our application, that does two things.
One, gives end users an ability to automate all of their manual
processes.

**Dave Wessinger:**
它能做两件事。第一，让最终用户能够自动化他们所有的手动流程。

**Dave Wessinger:** So they call it agents… Agent Operating Procedures.
And they're building a ton of them, on top of our application.

**Dave Wessinger:**
他们称之为智能体……智能体操作程序。他们在我们的应用程序之上构建了大量的这类程序。

**Dave Wessinger:** So what's interesting out of that is it's not… it's
not human-centered design. It's machine-centered design.

**Dave Wessinger:**
有趣的是，这不再是以人为本的设计，而是以机器为中心的设计。

**Dave Wessinger:** Kind of interesting. Um, kind of moving away from
that. And then where they've taken some opportunity, they've gone and
they've created Chrome extensions on top of our app to create a
side-by-side workflow where customers can create a lot of intelligence
in this Chrome extension.

**Dave Wessinger:**
这很有趣，有点偏离了传统模式。然后他们抓住了一些机会，在我们的应用之上创建了Chrome扩展程序，形成了一个并行的工作流，客户可以在这个Chrome扩展中创造出很多智能功能。

**Dave Wessinger:** On top of our application. So what's…. What's it?
And they're making really nice progress, kind of….

**Dave Wessinger:**
在我们的应用程序之上。所以……这是什么？他们正在取得非常好的进展，可以说……

**Dave Wessinger:** Let's say, to some extent, pre-revenue, but starting
to take off, because it's obviously solving a big problem.

**Dave Wessinger:**
在某种程度上，他们还处于营收前阶段，但已经开始起飞，因为它显然解决了一个大问题。

**Dave Wessinger:** And if it's not clear in every boardroom, the ask is
more AI, more AI, more AI, and so if somebody's solving that, and it's
not us, uh, that could be problematic, and so it does drive you to a
sense of urgency and pace to start to deliver on that need. So, two
different examples.

**Dave Wessinger:**
如果在每个董事会里还不清楚的话，那么需求就是更多的AI，更多的AI，更多的AI。所以如果有人在解决这个问题，而那个人不是我们，那可能会很麻烦。这确实会驱使你产生一种紧迫感和节奏感，去开始满足这种需求。所以，这是两个不同的例子。

**Dave Wessinger:** Of companies leveraging more of an AI. One wasn't
AI-native, and the other one is.

**Dave Wessinger:**
关于公司如何更多地利用AI。一个不是AI原生公司，另一个则是。

**Dave Wessinger:** Um, and then the question is, you know, how do you
compete against that, and how do you think about that?

**Dave Wessinger:** 那么问题来了，你如何与他们竞争，你如何看待这个问题？

**Dave Wessinger:** And then internally, think about this for a moment.
We're trying to deliver to our customers AI-powered solutions is where
we would like to be.

**Dave Wessinger:**
然后在内部，思考一下。我们希望能够为客户提供AI驱动的解决方案。

**Dave Wessinger:** Our vendors internally that you deal with, Alan, are
trying to.

**Dave Wessinger:** Alan，你所接触的我们内部的供应商，他们也在努力。

**Dave Wessinger:** Deliver AI to us, and they tend to be in their
segments, so whether it's finance, or sales, or product, or.

**Dave Wessinger:**
向我们提供AI，而且他们通常专注于各自的领域，无论是金融、销售、产品，还是其他。

**Dave Wessinger:** Or services, or otherwise. But we have to put Humpty
Dumpty together in some way, shape, or form to deliver a seamless
experience and process for our own employees, so….

**Dave Wessinger:**
或者是服务或其他方面。但我们必须以某种方式将这些零散的部分整合起来，为我们自己的员工提供无缝的体验和流程，所以……

**Dave Wessinger:** It's kind of hard to think about single-source AI
vendors. And that's why things like Copilot or orchestration layers take
off, is because they do go across so many different applications and
drive a ton of efficiency in the business, so….

**Dave Wessinger:**
很难想象只依赖单一来源的AI供应商。这就是为什么像Copilot或编排层这样的东西会流行起来，因为它们确实能够跨越许多不同的应用程序，并为业务带来巨大的效率提升，所以……

**Dave Wessinger:** There's just a few examples that, uh, have kind of
a….

**Dave Wessinger:** 这里只是几个例子，它们都有一种……

**Dave Wessinger:** It does drive a sense of urgency in terms of the….

**Dave Wessinger:** 它确实在……方面带来了一种紧迫感。

**Dave Wessinger:** These things aren't just… we're not just talking
about them in theory, they're real.

**Dave Wessinger:**
这些事情不仅仅是……我们不只是在理论上谈论它们，它们是真实存在的。

**Dave Wessinger:** They're starting to impact businesses. Uh, and its
material. Uh, so I think it's an opportunity internally, but also
externally. One doesn't go without the other.

**Dave Wessinger:**
它们已经开始影响企业，而且是实质性的影响。所以我认为这既是内部的机会，也是外部的机会。两者相辅相成。

**Alan Missen:** Yeah, those are great examples, Dave. I think your
point around, sort of.

**Alan Missen:** 是的，Dave，这些例子很棒。我认为你关于……的观点。

**Alan Missen:** You know, committed time to learn, right? And that sort
of ruthless prioritization.

**Alan Missen:**
你知道，投入时间去学习，对吧？以及那种坚决的优先级排序。

**Alan Missen:** The combination of those two, I think, is a very
powerful comment that we really need to take seriously on the back end
of today, frankly. I think it's a great point, well made.

**Alan Missen:**
我认为这两者的结合是一个非常有力的观点，坦白说，我们今天结束后真的需要认真对待。这是一个很好的观点，说得很好。

**Dave Wessinger:** Alan, how do you… let me ask you a question as we're
kind of going back and forth. We, as everybody here knows, or should
know, we've had a….

**Dave Wessinger:**
Alan，你如何……在我们来回讨论的时候，我问你一个问题。我们，在座的各位都知道，或者应该知道，我们有一个……

**Alan Missen:** Yeah, I think… I think we're kind of at the beginning
of the journey, um, in all honesty, but I… and I do think that that's
a….

**Alan Missen:**
是的，我认为……坦白说，我们才刚刚开始这段旅程，但我……我确实认为这是一个……

**Dave Wessinger:** A meaningful effort around P2C. And as you think
about what we're doing design-wise, business process engineering or
business process modeling.

**Dave Wessinger:**
围绕P2C（Product-to-Cash：从产品到现金，指企业从产品开发到最终收到客户付款的整个业务流程）的一项有意义的努力。当你思考我们在设计方面所做的工作，无论是业务流程工程还是业务流程建模。

**Dave Wessinger:** Is a lot around how humans use a solution, and we
think about, you know, Salesforce or other components that might be in
there, and NetSuite.

**Dave Wessinger:**
很多都是围绕人类如何使用一个解决方案，我们会考虑到Salesforce（赛富时：一家提供客户关系管理软件和服务的公司）或其他可能包含在内的组件，以及NetSuite（甲骨文公司旗下的云ERP软件）。

**Dave Wessinger:** How do you think about AI as it relates to designing
differently.

**Dave Wessinger:** 你如何看待AI在不同设计方法中的应用？

**Dave Wessinger:** For the things that we traditionally would focus on,
how does a human do X, and how do we make it better?

**Dave Wessinger:**
对于我们传统上关注的事情，比如人类如何完成某项任务X，以及我们如何改进它？

**Dave Wessinger:** How do you think differently about using agents, or
thinking differently about AI in just re-engineering the process?

**Dave Wessinger:**
在仅仅是重新设计流程方面，你对使用智能体或对AI有何不同的看法？

**Alan Missen:** An area we're evolving… we're trying to evolve quite…
quite quickly, Dave. I think….

**Alan Missen:**
Dave，这是一个我们正在努力……非常、非常快速发展的领域。我认为……

**Alan Missen:** If we look at, sort of, the traditional way to build…
to deliver those big transformational projects, you're right, you sort
of scope it, you build it, you test it, you go live.

**Alan Missen:**
如果我们看传统的方式来构建……来交付那些大型转型项目，你说得对，你通常是先确定范围，然后构建，测试，最后上线。

**Alan Missen:** And we're sort of two-thirds of the way down that
journey, and all of a sudden, there's a capability available to us that
wasn't when we started the project.

**Alan Missen:**
我们大概走完了这个过程的三分之二，然后突然之间，出现了一种我们项目开始时没有的能力。

**Dave Wessinger:** Yeah.

**Dave Wessinger:** 是的。

**Alan Missen:** Um, and so right now, we are sort of actively looking
at, are there 3 or 4 areas within P2C.

**Alan Missen:**
所以现在，我们正在积极地研究，在P2C（产品到现金）流程中是否有三到四个领域。

**Alan Missen:** That we can start leveraging this right away. So it's
not just about this new idea that's down the road that we'll go tackle.
It's like, we've got stuff that is in flight.

**Alan Missen:**
我们可以立即开始利用这项技术。所以这不仅仅是关于未来某个新想法，而是我们手头正在进行的项目。

**Alan Missen:** How do we start thinking about applying it right now?
So a great one is an….

**Alan Missen:** 我们如何开始思考立即应用它？一个很好的例子是……

**Alan Missen:** I think we showed it at the SLT, and I know it's a
passionate one for you, is….

**Alan Missen:** 我想我们在SLT（Senior Leadership
Team：高级领导团队）会议上展示过，而且我知道你对此充满热情，那就是……

**Alan Missen:** Could we get an agent to build a quote for a customer
for Go Live in November? Could we actually have that ready?

**Alan Missen:**
我们能否让一个智能体为客户在11月上线时生成一份报价？我们真的能准备好吗？

**Alan Missen:** Right? And so we're really kind of pushing the envelope
on that. And I think there's….

**Alan Missen:** 对吧？所以我们真的在挑战极限。而且我认为……

**Alan Missen:** 3 or 4 sort of agentic ideas, sort of on the back end
of the finance side.

**Alan Missen:** 在财务后端，有三到四个类似智能体的想法。

**Alan Missen:** As well, that we're starting to play around with is to
say, can we get those in for November 1st as well? So.

**Alan Missen:**
我们也开始尝试，看看能否在11月1日之前也把它们实现。所以。

**Alan Missen:** It's a little scary, because we're trying to, like,
change scope as we're sort of building the plane.

**Alan Missen:**
这有点吓人，因为我们就像是在造飞机的同时试图改变它的设计范围。

**Alan Missen:** Uh, but those are some of the things we're thinking
about, uh, within, say, say, PSC around that idea.

**Alan Missen:**
但这些是我们正在考虑的一些事情，比如在PSC（项目指导委员会）内部围绕这个想法进行讨论。

**Dave Wessinger:** Very good. Yeah, it's exciting. Your point is very
interesting in that….

**Dave Wessinger:** 非常好。是的，这很令人兴奋。你的观点非常有趣，在于……

**Dave Wessinger:** You know, the advancements in 6 months, never mind
24 hours.

**Dave Wessinger:** 你知道，六个月内的进步，更不用说24小时了。

**Dave Wessinger:** Are just… it's unsettling how… the pace of change,
and I think Mike talked about a 5-year time horizon.

**Dave Wessinger:**
简直是……变革的速度令人不安，我想Mike谈到了一个五年的时间跨度。

**Dave Wessinger:** Um, you know, disruption of the cloud really took
10-plus years.

**Dave Wessinger:** 你知道，云计算的颠覆真正花了十年以上的时间。

**Dave Wessinger:** Disruption here is…. Barely measured in years. I
mean, two, three years out, what we see today as normal is gonna be….

**Dave Wessinger:**
这里的颠覆……几乎不能用年来衡量。我的意思是，两三年后，我们今天视为正常的东西将会……

**Dave Wessinger:** It's gonna feel like it was 50 years ago history.
It's pretty incredible.

**Dave Wessinger:** 感觉就像是50年前的历史。这真是太不可思议了。

**Alan Missen:** Yeah. And I think the other comment you made, which is
really interesting, is some of the stuff that you're seeing around, sort
of, the bigger platforms, it's like the attack vector.

**Alan Missen:**
是的。而且我认为你提出的另一个评论也很有趣，就是你看到的一些关于大型平台的情况，它就像是攻击向量。

**Alan Missen:** For some of the innovations, actually, kind of on the
edges, right? It's not necessarily sort of the… always the big players
who are coming at you, it's the small, innovative.

**Alan Missen:**
对于一些创新来说，实际上是在边缘地带，对吧？不一定总是那些大公司来挑战你，而是那些小而创新的公司。

**Alan Missen:** Company that's sort of hitting it around the edges of
what sort of we're doing, and that's… that's really an interesting.

**Alan Missen:**
公司正在我们所做事情的边缘地带进行冲击，这……这确实是一个有趣的现象。

**Alan Missen:** Dynamic for us to wrap our head around. And then the
other comment you made around, sort of.

**Alan Missen:** 动态，需要我们去理解。然后你还提到了另一个评论，关于……

**Alan Missen:** How are the vendors in our space, our platform
partners, how are they playing?

**Alan Missen:**
我们领域的供应商，我们的平台合作伙伴，他们是如何参与竞争的？

**Alan Missen:** Um, there's a data point that's… there's a data point
that suggests right now.

**Alan Missen:** 有一个数据点……有一个数据点表明，现在。

**Alan Missen:** 80% of applications software plays. Will have AI
capabilities embedded in them.

**Alan Missen:** 80%的应用软件都将嵌入AI功能。

**Alan Missen:** By next year. By next year. So, wrapping your head
around sort of the rationalizations of which ones are good, which ones
can be integrated, which ones should we use.

**Alan Missen:**
到明年。到明年。所以，要理清哪些是好的，哪些可以集成，哪些我们应该使用，这需要好好思考。

## 用例展示：AI驱动的项目管理与洞察

### 用例1：Aakif Sheikh - 集成Copilot Studio与Power Automate的AI助手

**Aakif Shaik:** All right, thank you, Marina. Are you able to see my
screen?

**Aakif Shaik:** 好的，谢谢你，Marina。你能看到我的屏幕吗？

**Marina Stojanovic:** Thank you.

**Marina Stojanovic:** 谢谢。

**Marina Stojanovic:** I can see you! We cannot see your screen now.

**Marina Stojanovic:** 我能看到你！但现在我们看不到你的屏幕。

**Marina Stojanovic:** There we go! All right. Thanks, I keep… take it
away.

**Marina Stojanovic:** 好了！好的。谢谢，Akif……请开始吧。

**Aakif Shaik:** Okay, awesome. Sweet. Alright, hello everyone. My name
is Akif Sheikh. I am a business transformation co-op in the SDO.

**Aakif Shaik:** 好的，太棒了。很好。大家好。我叫Akif
Sheikh。我是SDO（战略交付办公室）的一名业务转型实习生。

**Aakif Shaik:** And over the past few weeks, I've been working on
building an AI-powered co-pilot agent that integrates with Copilot
Studio and Power Automate.

**Aakif Shaik:** 在过去几周里，我一直在致力于构建一个与Copilot
Studio和Power Automate集成的AI驱动的Copilot智能体。

**Aakif Shaik:** And for those of you who aren't familiar with AHA, it
is a product or a project management tool that teams use to be able to
track and manage their work.

**Aakif Shaik:**
对于那些不熟悉Aha!的人来说，它是一个产品或项目管理工具，团队用它来跟踪和管理他们的工作。

**Aakif Shaik:** And so, within the SDO, we essentially use AHA to track
and manage our key initiatives, like the go-to markets and the
product-to-cash program.

**Aakif Shaik:**
因此，在SDO内部，我们主要使用Aha!来跟踪和管理我们的关键举措，比如市场推广（go-to-market）和产品到现金（product-to-cash）项目。

**Aakif Shaik:** And so the problem that I was really focused on was,
how can I make it easier for people, whether they're a program manager
or someone within the team who's trying to access and get a quick
update, to be able to use an AI-powered assistant to do that. And so, if
you've ever found yourself thinking, hey, I just want a quick status
update without jumping between different tools.

**Aakif Shaik:**
我真正关注的问题是，如何让人们，无论是项目经理还是团队中试图获取快速更新的成员，能够更轻松地使用AI驱动的助手来完成这项工作。所以，如果你曾发现自己想，“嘿，我只想快速了解状态，而不想在不同工具之间切换”。

**Aakif Shaik:** Then this one's for you. And so, where we're at on our
current journey is, right at that pilot stage, where we're testing out
use cases.

**Aakif Shaik:**
那么这个就是为你准备的。我们目前的旅程正处于试点阶段，我们正在测试用例。

**Aakif Shaik:** As well as adding additional use cases, and so once we
get to that full functionality, is when we want to move to the full
adoption.

**Aakif Shaik:**
同时也在增加额外的用例，一旦我们实现了全部功能，我们就会转向全面采用。

**Aakif Shaik:** And so, going to the demo stage. Here is a little bit
of a walkthrough of what the UI interface looks like for Copilot Studio.

**Aakif Shaik:** 那么，进入演示阶段。这里是Copilot
Studio用户界面（UI）的一个简要介绍。

**Aakif Shaik:** And as you can see here, I'm going to start off by
giving it a simple prompt by asking it, hey, what are the activities
that are currently due this week?

**Aakif Shaik:**
正如你在这里看到的，我将从一个简单的提示开始，问它：“嘿，本周有哪些活动到期？”

**Aakif Shaik:** Right? And so, once I go ahead and do that, you can see
on the left side of the screen that it starts to execute a flow. And so
what this co-pilot agent is currently doing is using Power Automate,
which is integrated with Araha, to pull in information on activities
that are currently due this week.

**Aakif Shaik:**
对吧？一旦我这样做，你可以在屏幕左侧看到它开始执行一个流程。这个Copilot智能体目前正在做的是使用与Aha!集成的Power
Automate，来提取本周到期的活动信息。

**Aakif Shaik:** And so, here you go, it's particularly focused on GTM,
which is a go-to market program, and it shows us the names of the
activities due this week, along with their due dates.

**Aakif Shaik:**
好了，它特别关注GTM（Go-to-Market：市场推广）项目，并向我们显示了本周到期的活动名称及其截止日期。

**Aakif Shaik:** And this is great, and so let's say we want to take it
a little bit of a step further and say, hey, how can we go ahead and get
specific details for each of these activities, right? So I'm gonna go
ahead and give it another prompt now, asking it, I want to know the
status of a particular activity.

**Aakif Shaik:**
这很棒，那么让我们再进一步，说：“嘿，我们如何获取每个活动的具体细节？”对吧？所以我现在要给它另一个提示，问它：“我想知道某个特定活动的状态。”

**Aakif Shaik:** So, once again, you can see on the left side there,
it's executing a different flow now, um, which is asking for which
activity would I like to check. And so, I want to give it the name of
that particular activity.

**Aakif Shaik:**
所以，再次，你可以在左侧看到，它现在正在执行一个不同的流程，询问我想检查哪个活动。因此，我要告诉它那个特定活动的名称。

**Aakif Shaik:** And once I do that, that's when it starts to execute a
different flow.

**Aakif Shaik:** 一旦我这样做了，它就会开始执行一个不同的流程。

**Aakif Shaik:** And so now in this flow, the output is going to be
different, because it is going to be focused on this particular activity
and getting us the status updates. So here we go, gives us the name,
what the current status is.

**Aakif Shaik:**
所以现在在这个流程中，输出将会不同，因为它将专注于这个特定的活动并为我们获取状态更新。好了，它给出了名称，当前的状态是什么。

**Aakif Shaik:** What the due date is, as well as who it is assigned to.

**Aakif Shaik:** 截止日期是什么，以及分配给了谁。

**Aakif Shaik:** And so, this is what the current functionality of the
agent looks like, and so going a little bit of what's under the hood.

**Aakif Shaik:**
这就是这个智能体当前的功能。现在我们来看看它的内部工作原理。

**Aakif Shaik:** If you want to add additional functionalities, you
essentially add them as topics until you start off with a trigger, and
then a question.

**Aakif Shaik:**
如果你想添加额外的功能，你基本上是将它们作为主题添加，直到你从一个触发器开始，然后是一个问题。

**Aakif Shaik:** And then the action. So this is where you want to
integrate your Power Automate flow with it. And lastly, you have your
output message.

**Aakif Shaik:** 然后是动作。这就是你想要将Power
Automate流程与之集成的地方。最后，你会有你的输出信息。

**Aakif Shaik:** And so the same thing goes, um, you know, for the other
flow as well, which covers what is due this week. And so, this trigger
is really important because this is what the agent uses to differentiate
on what your ask is.

**Aakif Shaik:**
同样地，对于另一个流程也是如此，它涵盖了本周到期的任务。这个触发器非常重要，因为智能体用它来区分你的请求是什么。

**Aakif Shaik:** And so, um, once again, you have your flow, as well as
your final message. And so, for those of you that are curious to see,
you know, what this Power Automate flow looks like, feel free to reach
out, and I'll be happy to give you a walkthrough after this call as
well.

**Aakif Shaik:**
所以，再次，你有你的流程，以及你的最终信息。对于那些好奇想看看这个Power
Automate流程是什么样子的朋友，请随时联系我，我很乐意在这次通话后也给你们做一个演示。

**Aakif Shaik:** So now, moving on to, you know, really talking about
impact, right? And so what this tool really allows teams to do is
transform how they access project updates. So having this AI-powered
assistant allows you to just, you know, minimize the use of switching
over different tools, as well as digging through different dashboards.

**Aakif Shaik:**
现在，我们来谈谈影响，对吧？这个工具真正让团队能够改变他们获取项目更新的方式。拥有这个AI驱动的助手，可以让你减少在不同工具之间切换的次数，以及在不同仪表盘中挖掘信息的麻烦。

**Aakif Shaik:** And actually just be able to get detailed, focused
answers through a simple question.

**Aakif Shaik:** 并且能够通过一个简单的问题获得详细、集中的答案。

**Aakif Shaik:** Now, the lessons learned for me in this journey were
definitely to start small and build iteratively. So following up on what
Dave had said earlier, it was, you know, starting off with a simple use
case, testing out a sample set of data, and continuously building on
that to make sure that it didn't get overwhelmed.

**Aakif Shaik:**
在这次旅程中，我学到的教训绝对是從小處著手，迭代構建。接續Dave之前所說的，就是從一個簡單的用例開始，測試一組樣本數據，並在此基礎上不斷構建，以確保不會不堪重負。

**Aakif Shaik:** And then, you know, getting to the stage where we're
at, where we're working with all of the complex data.

**Aakif Shaik:**
然后，你知道，进入我们现在的阶段，我们正在处理所有复杂的数据。

**Aakif Shaik:** Now, how we can help others at PCC, so teams can
definitely use, um, you know, Copilot agents for various purposes, and
so one thing I can think of would be for the product team to be able to,
you know, build a co-pilot agent that integrates with their product
roadmap, so that teams can get status of where they're at in the entire
product roadmap journey.

**Aakif Shaik:**
现在，我们如何能帮助PCC（PointClickCare）的其他人，团队绝对可以出于各种目的使用Copilot智能体。我能想到的一个例子是，产品团队可以构建一个与他们的产品路线图集成的Copilot智能体，这样团队就能了解他们在整个产品路线图旅程中的进展状态。

**Aakif Shaik:** This can also be useful for teams that use Jira, so be
able to get quick status updates on what the JIRA, um, you know.

**Aakif Shaik:**
这对于使用Jira（一款流行的项目管理和问题跟踪软件）的团队也很有用，可以快速获取Jira的状态更新。

**Aakif Shaik:** Dashboard basically states. And lastly, the responsible
use of AI. So, this project aligns with the responsible AI guidelines.

**Aakif Shaik:**
仪表盘基本上显示了什么。最后，是负责任地使用AI。这个项目符合负责任AI的指导方针。

**Aakif Shaik:** Because it focuses on transparency and user control.
The co-pilot agent that you saw earlier delivers clear information
directly from AHA without actually, you know, making any decisions on
behalf of the user. And it does this accurate information.

**Aakif Shaik:**
因为它注重透明度和用户控制。你之前看到的Copilot智能体直接从Aha!提供清晰的信息，而不会代表用户做出任何决定。它提供的是准确的信息。

**Aakif Shaik:** And make sure that there is no bias in the response as

**Aakif Shaik:**

**Pam Martin:**

**Pam Martin:** 当我们在Outlook中使用Copilot时，我们还可以利用Gainsight

account-level timeline, and it captures everything that happens in the

**Pam Martin:**
所以时间线，我们现在看到的是一个账户级别的时间线，它记录了账户中发生的一切。

**Pam Martin:** 这里没有AI的魔力。我们马上就会讲到。

**Pam Martin:**
但它的作用是捕捉所有这些活动，让我们全面了解账户中发生的情况。

**Pam Martin:**
所以无论是他们收到的程序化信息，还是他们如何管理账户风险，管理NPS（净推荐值）的批评者。

**Pam Martin:** 那些发布在那里的会议。所有这些都会进入时间线。

**Pam Martin:** So now, this is an account view, and you can see how

**Pam Martin:**
所以现在，这是一个账户视图，你可以看到它能创造出多么丰富的信息。

**Pam Martin:** And if without AI cheat sheet, you have to go through
every single one of those to see what's going on.

**Pam Martin:**
如果没有AI备忘单，你必须逐一查看所有这些信息才能了解情况。

**Pam Martin:** But, with AI cheat sheet, it gives us a summary of the
last 6 months of what's happening at that account level.

**Pam Martin:**
但是，有了AI备忘单，它为我们提供了过去6个月在该账户级别发生的事情的摘要。

**Pam Martin:** And this is really powerful, because it eliminates the
recency effect, where people often only reflect on.

**Pam Martin:**
这非常强大，因为它消除了近因效应，即人们通常只反思最近发生的事情。

**Pam Martin:** You know, our memory goes back only so far, because
we're all so busy. So you're thinking about, oh, what happened last
week? What happened last month?

**Pam Martin:**
你知道，我们的记忆只能追溯到一定程度，因为我们都太忙了。所以你会想，哦，上周发生了什么？上个月发生了什么？

**Pam Martin:** And a lot of times after that, it gets lost, so it pulls
out some really key information in here that's valuable for the CSM.

**Pam Martin:**
很多时候，之后的信息就丢失了，所以它从中提取了一些对客户成功经理（CSM）非常有价值的关键信息。

**Pam Martin:** But even valuable in how we use this cross-functionally.
So we have other teams that can then… we can share this with them.

**Pam Martin:**
但在我们跨职能使用它时也很有价值。所以我们有其他团队可以……我们可以与他们分享这个。

**Pam Martin:** So think about if we have an escalation, if we have a
customer who wants, um, to discuss product, um, we can pull this.

**Pam Martin:**
所以想一想，如果我们有升级事件，如果我们有客户想要讨论产品，我们可以提取这个。

**Pam Martin:** Summary of the account and share it with them. So, the…
as we're looking at this.

**Pam Martin:** 账户摘要并与他们分享。所以，当我们看这个的时候。

**Pam Martin:** We do ask the CSMs to look at this and think about what
they're seeing critically. Does it cover all the right information? Is
there anything that's missing here?

**Pam Martin:**
我们确实要求客户成功经理（CSM）审视这个，并批判性地思考他们看到了什么。它是否涵盖了所有正确的信息？这里是否有什么遗漏？

**Pam Martin:** And so, they do have the option of adding notes to it if
they feel like it's not accurately giving the full picture.

**Pam Martin:**

### 用例3 & 4：Sonal Misra - Azure OpenAI在市场营销中的应用

GPT。

**Sonal Misra:** 大家好。我是Sonal

**Sonal Misra:** So, using Azure's OpenAI, I engineered custom prompts

**Sonal Misra:** 把Azure
OpenAI想象成一个人的数字版“布朗博士”（电影《回到未来》中的角色），高度智能，思维敏捷，还有点未来感。

**Sonal Misra:**

**Sonal Misra:**

**Sonal Misra:** Into structured, actionable insights. This approach
replaces manual analysis with automated extraction of key elements, such
as customer challenges, value statements, and impactment.

**Sonal Misra:**
转化为结构化、可操作的洞察。这种方法用自动化提取关键元素，如客户挑战、价值陈述和影响指标，取代了手动分析。

**Sonal Misra:** Metrics. Over here in the chat playground, I have
inputted. The interview transcript collected from the interview.

**Sonal Misra:**
指标。在这里的聊天操场上，我输入了从访谈中收集的访谈记录。

**Sonal Misra:** And in order to highlight, for example, the customer
challenges, I inputted the prompt asking it to highlight specific
problems, inefficiencies, or frustrations.

**Sonal Misra:**
为了突出客户挑战，我输入了提示，要求它突出显示客户在采用产品之前面临的具体问题、低效率或挫败感。

**Sonal Misra:** That the customer faced before the adoption of the
product. Thereby, the model was able to identify codes above manual
broaden, higher ed risk, and inefficient workflows, which are kind of
insights that the team can act immediately upon.

**Sonal Misra:**
客户在采用该产品之前所面临的问题。因此，该模型能够识别出超越手动范围的代码、更高的风险和低效的工作流程，这些都是团队可以立即采取行动的洞察。

**Sonal Misra:** Next, in order to identify solution and product value,
I asked it to extract descriptions on how it… the solution improved the
workflow.

**Sonal Misra:**
接下来，为了识别解决方案和产品价值，我要求它提取关于解决方案如何改进工作流程的描述。

**Sonal Misra:** Anyway, the model was able to put out value-driven
quotes that.

**Sonal Misra:** 总之，该模型能够输出价值驱动的引言。

**Sonal Misra:** Such as how there was seamless information sharing,
reduced medication errors, increase in efficiency for care staff.

**Sonal Misra:**
例如，如何实现无缝信息共享，减少用药错误，提高护理人员的效率。

**Sonal Misra:** All wonderful things that are great for case studies
and marketing material.

**Sonal Misra:**
所有这些都是非常棒的东西，非常适合用于案例研究和市场营销材料。

**Sonal Misra:** Furthermore, in order to identify the metrics and proof
points. I was able to input the prompt asking you to list on numeric
evidence or performance indicators that was provided in the interview.

**Sonal Misra:**
此外，为了识别指标和证据点，我能够输入提示，要求你列出访谈中提供的数字证据或绩效指标。

**Sonal Misra:** Thereby, it was able to capture. The number of years
that the organization had been with Pointed Care.

**Sonal Misra:** 因此，它能够捕捉到该组织与PointClickCare合作的年数。

**Sonal Misra:** I'll get started off at one location, and have expanded
to over 50 locations. The reduction in call times, and such are the
wonderful metrics from the interview task.

**Sonal Misra:**
我将从一个地点开始，并已扩展到超过50个地点。通话时间的减少，以及诸如此类的，都是访谈任务中得出的精彩指标。

**Sonal Misra:** Transcription. Lastly, in order to identify value
quotes and testimonials. I included the prompt asking it to extract.

**Sonal Misra:**
转录。最后，为了识别有价值的引言和客户评价，我加入了要求它提取的提示。

**Sonal Misra:** The scene. It was able to capture each quote that
they're in.

**Sonal Misra:** 场景。它能够捕捉到他们所在的每一个引言。

**Sonal Misra:** The input that the customer was able to mention. For
every graduate degree leading from.

**Sonal Misra:** 客户能够提及的输入。对于每一个从……

**Sonal Misra:** The current patient and resident care, to reducing
medication errors, which could be used for, again, marketing materials.

**Sonal Misra:**
当前的病人和居民护理，到减少用药错误，这些都可以再次用于市场营销材料。

**Sonal Misra:** Uh, and customer testimonials. In conclusion, I was
able to develop a full prompt library, categorized by theme, based upon
customer challenges, solution, and value, metrics improve.

**Sonal Misra:**
以及客户评价。总而言之，我能够开发一个完整的提示库，按主题分类，基于客户挑战、解决方案和价值、指标改进。

**Sonal Misra:** Testimonials. All of these templates that can be reused
across transcripts, which are adapted for fine-tuning, or can be
embedded in search pipelines.

**Sonal Misra:**
客户评价。所有这些模板都可以在不同的转录稿中重复使用，它们可以被调整以进行微调，或者可以嵌入到搜索管道中。

**Sonal Misra:** And reducing manual review time by over 50%.

**Sonal Misra:** 并将手动审查时间减少了50%以上。

**Sonal Misra:** So, the project is aimed to deliver high-impact results
where we significantly reduce analysis time.

**Sonal Misra:**
所以，这个项目旨在交付高影响力的结果，我们显著减少了分析时间。

**Sonal Misra:** By eliminating this need to sift through lengthy
interview transcripts. The extracted insights are now consistent,
quickly accessible, and easily reusable across different themes, such as
marketing, sales, and product teams.

**Sonal Misra:**
通过消除筛选冗长访谈记录的需求。提取的洞察现在是一致的、可快速访问的，并且可以轻松地在不同主题中重复使用，例如市场、销售和产品团队。

**Sonal Misra:** Furthermore, this ensures that the quality of the
content has improved with more accurate quotes.

**Sonal Misra:** 此外，这确保了内容质量的提高，引言更准确。

**Sonal Misra:** Clearer themes and less reliance on manual
interpretation. Now, you may wonder how others might be able to use
this.

**Sonal Misra:**
主题更清晰，对人工解读的依赖更少。现在，你可能会想知道其他人如何使用这个。

**Sonal Misra:** The best part is, this approach is easily adaptable for
any team working with qualitative feedback.

**Sonal Misra:**
最好的部分是，这种方法很容易适用于任何处理定性反馈的团队。

**Sonal Misra:** Marketing, for example, can potentially extract
compelling value quotes. Project teams can be… can surface recurring
pain points, and sales can possibly identify impactful success metrics.

**Sonal Misra:**
例如，市场营销可以提取引人注目的价值引言。项目团队可以……可以发现反复出现的痛点，而销售团队则可能识别出有影响力的成功指标。

**Sonal Misra:** All using same set of prompts, templates. Whether
analyzing surveys, interviews, or feedback forms, where this method
helps streamline and enhance insight generation across boards.

**Sonal Misra:**
全部使用同一套提示和模板。无论是分析调查、访谈还是反馈表，这种方法都有助于全面简化和增强洞察的生成。

**Sonal Misra:** While creating this project, I also focused upon the
fact that I was using AI responsibly, so these prompts were tested and
results were manually validated.

**Sonal Misra:**
在创建这个项目时，我也注重负责任地使用AI，所以这些提示都经过了测试，结果也经过了手动验证。

**Sonal Misra:** We prioritize explainability, use of neutral language
to avoid bias, and ensured humans remain entirely in control, so there
were no rogue AIs rewriting our past, like Biffs with a stolen sports
almanac.

**Sonal Misra:**
我们优先考虑可解释性，使用中性语言以避免偏见，并确保人类完全掌控，所以没有像《回到未来》中拿着被盗体育年鉴的Biff那样，有流氓AI改写我们的过去。

**Sonal Misra:** Um, when you use responsibility. As Doc Brown would say

### 主持人互动：AI的法律责任

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** Hi, everyone! So, while we're waiting for our
next presenter to get set up, I have a question for all of you.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
大家好！在我们等待下一位演讲者准备的时候，我有一个问题要问大家。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** So, fact or fiction? Ai can be held legally
responsible. Tell me in the chat what you think the answer is.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
事实还是虚构？AI可以承担法律责任。在聊天中告诉我你认为答案是什么。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** I wish I had some Jeopardy music. Oh, yeah, not
yet. False, not true, fiction, no.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
我希望我有一些《危险边缘》的音乐。哦，是的，还没有。假的，不是真的，虚构的，不。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** Somebody said, Drew, I'm seeing a lot of
fiction, no way.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** 有人说，Drew，我看到了很多虚构的东西，不可能。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** Pilot of AI, true AI, nope. Okay! Lots of
really interesting responses, but it seems… can you sue AI, Marina's
asking. Okay, so….

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
AI的试点，真正的AI，不。好的！很多非常有趣的回答，但似乎……你能起诉AI吗，Marina在问。好的，所以……

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** If you haven't responded yet, and you're
thinking about the question, we will tell you what the answer is.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
如果你还没有回答，并且正在思考这个问题，我们会告诉你答案是什么。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** The answer is that this is fiction. Um, AI is
not a separate legal entity, so it can't be held responsible.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
答案是，这是虚构的。AI不是一个独立的法律实体，所以它不能承担责任。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** And there's actually really interesting stories
about this in the news over the last few years. One of the ones that
sticks out for me is a story about Air Canada and its chatbot.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
过去几年新闻里其实有很多关于这个的有趣故事。其中一个让我印象深刻的是关于加拿大航空公司及其聊天机器人的故事。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** Keki, do you remember hearing that story?

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** Keki，你记得听过那个故事吗？

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Yeah, I vaguely remember something. It was in the
news, wasn't it?

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 是的，我模糊地记得一些。它上过新闻，不是吗？

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** Yes, I was. Okay, so basically what happened
was, in 2022, Air Canada had a chatbot on its website.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
是的，我记得。好的，基本上是这样的，2022年，加拿大航空公司在其网站上有一个聊天机器人。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** And a customer went in and asked about a
particular discount. The chatbot said that it could be honored.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
一位顾客进去询问一个特定的折扣。聊天机器人说可以兑现。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** But it turns out that Air Canada said that it
shouldn't. And so they wouldn't want to honor the discount, and when
they were taken to court.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
但结果是加拿大航空公司说不应该兑现。所以他们不想兑现这个折扣，当他们被起诉到法庭时。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** The court actually ruled against them. They
basically said, it's your website, the chatbot's on your website, so
you're responsible for whatever it puts out. And so then they were
required to not only pay.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
法院实际上判他们败诉。他们基本上说，这是你们的网站，聊天机器人在你们的网站上，所以你们要对它发布的一切负责。因此，他们不仅被要求支付。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** What the difference was, but also legal fees,
etc. So, I think the story behind this is that.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
差价，还要支付律师费等。所以，我认为这背后的故事是。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** As you're using AI, and, you know, we're
talking about chatbots, we have another one coming up soon.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
当你使用AI时，你知道，我们正在谈论聊天机器人，我们很快就会有另一个。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** You want to make sure it's trained on the
appropriate information so that it's pulling the right content when
someone asks a question.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
你要确保它接受了适当信息的训练，这样当有人提问时，它能提取正确的内容。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** And then in general, when you're using AI, you
want to make sure you're validating the output before you use it. And
you'll hear us talk about RAI throughout all of them.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
总的来说，当你使用AI时，你要确保在使用之前验证输出。你会听到我们在所有这些中都谈到RAI（负责任的AI）。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** Uh, yeah, Mike, we actually were gonna speak to
that story next, uh, about this notorious legal incident. So, Keck, you
want to tell us a little bit about that?

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
是的，Mike，我们接下来就要讲那个故事，关于这个臭名昭著的法律事件。所以，Keck，你想给我们讲讲吗？

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Yeah. Oh, yeah! Yeah, that was a very interesting
incident. I remember, uh, there was a notorious legal incident from
2023, uh, where a New York lawyer who used ChatGPT to draft a court
filing.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
是的。哦，是的！是的，那是一个非常有趣的事件。我记得，2023年有一个臭名昭著的法律事件，一位纽约律师使用ChatGPT起草了一份法庭文件。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** And he actually ended up citing 6 completely
fabricated legal cases. All of these cases were hallucinated.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
他最终引用了6个完全捏造的法律案例。所有这些案例都是AI幻觉的结果。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** And what we mean by hallucination, AI does that
quite a bit, is that they were completely made up by AI, they just did
not exist.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
我们所说的幻觉，AI经常这样做，就是它们完全是AI编造出来的，根本不存在。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** And the judge had to sanction the lawyer. The
courts even emphasized that while using AI, which is not inherently
wrong, lawyers do have a duty to verify the accuracy of their filing and
what they are citing.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
法官不得不制裁这位律师。法院甚至强调，虽然使用AI本身并没有错，但律师有责任核实他们提交文件的准确性以及他们引用的内容。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Uh, in those filings. So it was a very, very
interesting incident, and both the lawyer and his colleague were
actually sanctioned in that case.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
在那些文件中。所以这是一个非常、非常有趣的事件，在那起案件中，律师和他的同事都受到了制裁。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** They also had to pay a penalty. So yeah, very
interesting case.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 他们还必须支付罚款。所以是的，非常有趣的案例。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** With great power comes great responsibility,

your point, Tim, you want the human in the loop, right? That's a really
important part as we use AI.

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**
能力越大，责任越大，对吧？虽然是另一部电影，但在这里也挺相关的。是的，Tim，你说得对，你需要有人在环（human

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Yeah.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 是的。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**

**Mary Henschel:** Just how much of our product is dependent on meeting

**Mary Henschel:** 我们的产品在多大程度上依赖于满足法规。这非常多。

**Mary Henschel:** And so our team reads, uh, we influence, we

**Mary Henschel:** 所以我们的团队阅读、影响、解释、翻译法规。

**Mary Henschel:**

**Mary Henschel:** 我们的问题。有太多的法规需要我们去应对。

**Mary Henschel:**

**Mary Henschel:** 正如我所说，法规团队相对较小，所以我们需要一种方法。

**Mary Henschel:**

**Mary Henschel:** So, we currently have a regulatory repository, uh,

**Mary Henschel:**
所以我们从去年夏天开始研究解决方案。我们考察了几款商业AI产品，但没有一款能解决我们最大的挑战，那就是知道法规何时更新。

**Mary Henschel:** So all the other commercial tools. Put the onus on us

**Mary Henschel:**

**Mary Henschel:**
来研究这个挑战。那么，我们来看看第一部分。我要讲的是第一部分，也就是问题的前端，即弄清楚法规何时更新。

**Mary Henschel:** 所以，我向Rahim团队的Amandeep

**Mary Henschel:**

**Mary Henschel:**

**Hazelle Florencio:**

**Hazelle Florencio:** Uh, which means that your answers, or the answers

**Hazelle Florencio:** 这意味着你得到的答案是基于可信和干净的数据。

**Mary Henschel:**

**Mary Henschel:** May be incorrect. And so that's part of our

**Mary Henschel:** 可能不正确。所以这是我们负责任地使用AI的一部分。

**Mary Henschel:** And then it also gives me the two references, because

**Mary Henschel:**

information in the source.

**Mary Henschel:**

**Mary Henschel:** 然后……我要再深入一点，看看实际的州法规。

**Mary Henschel:** 网站，呃……所以我得到……

**Mary Henschel:** It's really hard. There's the language.

**Mary Henschel:** 这真的很难。有语言障碍。

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:** Mary, do you want to try it one more time with

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**

**Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq:**

**Mary Henschel:** Well, that was…. That was too bad. Anyways, the way
it works is it essentially.

**Mary Henschel:** 嗯，那……那太糟糕了。总之，它的工作方式基本上是。

**Mary Henschel:** Uh, it is continually updating, making sure that we
have the best, uh, and most up-to-date, uh, regulations.

**Mary Henschel:** 它在持续更新，确保我们拥有最好、最新的法规。

**Mary Henschel:** We can ask them questions, we can validate it. And

**Mary Henschel:**

**Mary Henschel:** 然后我们给它一个差评。并且，我们说明为什么它不正确。

**Mary Henschel:**

**Mary Henschel:** 到目前为止，结果非常令人兴奋，而且……

**Mary Henschel:**

## 主题演讲：Alan Missen - AI的经济影响、企业应用与未来战略

**Alan Missen:** 好的？现在呢？太棒了。好的。

**Alan Missen:** So I started the day a little bit with those quotes,

市场。去年年底，相关公司的总市值约为五千亿美元，也就是几个月前。

about 37% a year. I've been a lot… this is industry 11 for me.

projected contribution that's gonna make.

**Alan Missen:** 非常引人入胜。当我们审视它预计将做出的贡献时。

**Alan Missen:**

combined. So it's a massive component of what's coming around. So.

**Alan Missen:**

around, is this fad. This is clearly not a fad.

**Alan Missen:**

**Alan Missen:** Um, in terms of productivity, the expectation is that
AI should improve employee productivity by at least 40% in the coming.

**Alan Missen:**
在生产力方面，预期AI将在未来几年内将员工生产力提高至少40%。

this, is the value.

**Alan Missen:**
在未来几年。另一个非常有趣的点，因为很多组织都在为此挣扎，那就是价值。

**Alan Missen:** Around it, the ROI around it. Um, it's been a bit
tricky at times, particularly with some of the utility tools, like
Copilot. You give somebody 15, 20, 30 minutes of time back a day. How

**Alan Missen:** 围绕它的价值，它的投资回报率（ROI：Return on

**Alan Missen:** True value for an organization, because you can't
necessarily point at it in a P&L.

**Alan Missen:** 对组织的真正价值，因为你未必能在一个损益表（P&L：Profit

Around what they're using AI for are starting to see a turnaround in the
ROI equation. So 74% of organizations.

**Alan Missen:**
但是，那些非常有针对性地使用AI的组织，已经开始在投资回报率方面看到转机。74%的组织。

**Alan Missen:** Um, they're using some more advanced AI initiatives,
are meeting or exceeding their ROI expectations, and 20% of those ROIs.

**Alan Missen:**
他们正在使用一些更先进的AI举措，达到了或超过了他们的投资回报率预期，而其中20%的投资回报率。

**Alan Missen:** Are actually greater than 30%. So I think that sort of
points to us really being thoughtful. I love the experimentation and the
breadth of the types of things we're playing with, but.

**Alan Missen:**
实际上超过了30%。所以我认为这表明我们真的需要深思熟虑。我喜欢实验和我们正在尝试的各种事物的广度，但是。

**Alan Missen:** Part of our journey, I do think, is sort of the
prioritization of the ones that are going to be the most meaningful to
the business.

**Alan Missen:**
我确实认为，我们旅程的一部分，是对那些对业务最有意义的事情进行优先级排序。

**Alan Missen:** Um, and then, you know, Dave talked a little bit about
this as well. Ai is very, very quickly become the top funded.

**Alan Missen:**
然后，你知道，Dave也稍微谈到了这一点。AI已经非常、非常迅速地成为资金最充裕的领域。

**Alan Missen:** Sector, right? Already one-third of VC funding.

**Alan Missen:** 行业，对吧？已经有三分之一的风险投资（VC：Venture
Capital）资金。

**Alan Missen:** Is going directly towards AI-related companies in
really a very, very short time. So for it to become the number one
sector.

**Alan Missen:**
在非常、非常短的时间内直接流向了与AI相关的公司。所以它能成为第一大行业。

**Alan Missen:** In literally the space of the year is fascinating. Um,
if I look at the next dynamic around, sort of, usage, and this is really
more of a business usage lens.

**Alan Missen:**
在短短一年内就实现，这真是令人着迷。如果我看一下下一个关于使用情况的动态，这更多的是从商业使用的角度来看。

**Alan Missen:** Um, adoption, um, for business… businesses, uh, by the
end of 24 was about 72% of businesses were reporting.

**Alan Missen:** 到24年底，商业领域的采用率大约为72%的企业报告称。

**Alan Missen:** You know, using AI and at least one function. Um, and
that's a significant leap over 2023. Gen AI, similarly, the adoption has
soared.

**Alan Missen:**
至少在一个职能上使用AI。这比2023年有了显著的飞跃。同样，生成式AI的采用率也飙升了。

**Alan Missen:** Um, with about 50% of businesses using them by the end
of 2024.

**Alan Missen:** 到2024年底，约有50%的企业在使用它们。

**Alan Missen:** And that's up 33% from 2023. So the acceleration of
use, and we're seeing that, Rahim and I are seeing that.

**Alan Missen:**
这比2023年增长了33%。所以使用的加速，我们看到了，Rahim和我也看到了。

**Alan Missen:** With some of the tools that we've got in place around
Copilot, we're seeing a very aggressive.

**Alan Missen:**
通过我们围绕Copilot部署的一些工具，我们看到了非常积极的增长。

**Alan Missen:** Utilization number sort of growing. And just for

**Alan Missen:** 对，所以我把它归结为，这实际上是一个组合。

applying AI tools to it. So I think that's another big part, as we sort
of evolved this AI-first culture that we need to be thoughtful about.

**Alan Missen:** 拥有精益六西格玛（Lean Six

**Alan Missen:**

**Alan Missen:**

## 下午场：深入探讨组织影响与AI应用

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Welcome back, everyone! I hope you had a really
delicious lunch, and I hope it wasn't AI-generated.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
欢迎回来，各位！希望你们享用了一顿非常美味的午餐，也希望它不是AI生成的。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Um, but I'm wondering if any of the recipes were,
though. If yes, please tell us in the chat.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
但我在想，有没有食谱是AI生成的呢？如果有，请在聊天中告诉我们。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Um, also, if you are joining us just now, please
use the QR code at the bottom left corner of the screen.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
另外，如果你是刚刚加入我们，请使用屏幕左下角的二维码。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** And tell us a little bit more about your AI
journey. It's a very simple survey with very few questions, but it'll
really help us.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
并告诉我们更多关于你的AI旅程。这是一个非常简单的调查，只有几个问题，但它真的能帮助我们。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Um, get some of the data from you. So please take a
moment to….

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 从你那里获取一些数据。所以请花点时间……

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Scan the QR code and answer a few questions. We'll
just give everyone a few minutes to be back.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
扫描二维码并回答几个问题。我们给大家几分钟时间回来。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Okay, and, uh…. We're diving into more use cases
now.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 好的，现在……我们开始深入探讨更多的用例。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Starting with Caleb and Christy from the Security
and Trust team.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 从安全与信任团队的Caleb和Christy开始。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** They will be talking to us about ReliaQuest gray
matter agentic AI.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 他们将向我们介绍ReliaQuest灰质智能体AI（ReliaQuest
GreyMatter：一个集成了安全运营和AI技术的平台）。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Extra points for anyone that can say this 5 times
fast.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 谁能快速说五遍这个名字，可以加分。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** So, over to you, Caleb and Christy.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 那么，交给你们了，Caleb和Christy。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Are you able to share your screen? I'm gonna stop
sharing now.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 你能分享你的屏幕吗？我现在要停止分享了。

### 用例6：Caleb Waldemar & Kristy Liu - ReliaQuest灰质智能体AI

**Caleb Waldemar:** Yep, Chrissy should be getting it shared in a second
here.

**Caleb Waldemar:** 是的，Chrissy马上就会分享出来。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Amazing.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 太棒了。

**kristy liu:** All right, um, yep. Uh, so my name is Christy, I'm here
with Caleb. We're both from the security operations team.

**kristy liu:**
好的，是的。我叫Christy，我和Caleb一起。我们都来自安全运营团队。

**Caleb Waldemar:** There you are, Christy.

**Caleb Waldemar:** 你来了，Christy。

**kristy liu:** We focus on phishing emails and different types of
investigation that involves users and endpoints.

**kristy liu:** 我们专注于网络钓鱼邮件以及涉及用户和终端的各种调查。

**kristy liu:** Things like suspicious login account issues, or anything
unusual happening on devices.

**kristy liu:** 比如可疑的登录账户问题，或者设备上发生的任何异常情况。

**kristy liu:** Today, we're going to talk about how we've been using
Agentech AI to speed up and simplify the threat detections.

**kristy liu:**
今天，我们将讨论我们如何使用智能体AI来加速和简化威胁检测。

**kristy liu:** So, looking at this slide, you can see just how many
different tools we use on a daily basis.

**kristy liu:**
所以，看这张幻灯片，你可以看到我们每天使用多少种不同的工具。

**kristy liu:** Uh, we use platforms like Defender, Crowd, Sentinel,
Wiz, and Mindcast.

**kristy liu:**
我们使用像Defender、CrowdStrike、Sentinel、Wiz和Mimecast这样的平台。

**kristy liu:** They're all important to our work, but each one has its
own interface, and each tool shows data in a different way.

**kristy liu:**
它们对我们的工作都很重要，但每个都有自己的界面，每个工具以不同的方式显示数据。

**kristy liu:** And this means investigation can take longer because we
need to pivot back and forth.

**kristy liu:** 这意味着调查可能需要更长的时间，因为我们需要来回切换。

**kristy liu:** Sometimes we need to run multiple queries in different
platforms and try to piece everything together manually.

**kristy liu:**
有时我们需要在不同的平台上运行多个查询，并尝试手动将所有信息拼凑在一起。

**kristy liu:** We realized the challenge, and we can do something to
improve it. Therefore, we purchased ReliaQuest.

**kristy liu:**
我们意识到了这个挑战，并且我们可以做些什么来改进它。因此，我们购买了ReliaQuest。

**kristy liu:** And we feed all the log sources into ReliaQuest. Now
relyQuest becomes the central platform. It posts the data from all these
tools, and it uses AI to normalize the data.

**kristy liu:**
我们将所有的日志源输入到ReliaQuest中。现在ReliaQuest成为了中心平台。它发布来自所有这些工具的数据，并使用AI来规范化数据。

**kristy liu:** And we can just work from one place. Because of that,
investigation time has dropped from 45 minutes.

**kristy liu:** 我们就可以在一个地方工作。因此，调查时间从45分钟减少了。

**kristy liu:** Down to about 20 minutes in many cases. We now have
reusable playbooks and clear process in place that makes it easier for
anyone on the team, regardless their new or experienced.

**kristy liu:**
在许多情况下，降至约20分钟。我们现在有了可重复使用的剧本和清晰的流程，这使得团队中的任何人，无论他们是新手还是经验丰富，都能更容易地工作。

**kristy liu:** This slide shows how ReliaQuest uses Agenta AI to
investigate alerts.

**kristy liu:** 这张幻灯片展示了ReliaQuest如何使用智能体AI来调查警报。

**kristy liu:** When an alert comes in, the process starts with the
planner component.

**kristy liu:** 当警报传来时，流程从规划器组件开始。

**kristy liu:** It's like the brain of the system. Uh, it looks at the
context around the alert.

**kristy liu:** 它就像系统的大脑。它会查看警报的上下文。

**kristy liu:** It knows the environment, and if there are any similar
past alerts, and so on.

**kristy liu:** 它了解环境，以及是否有任何类似的过去警报等等。

**kristy liu:** Then it will decide how to investigate it. After the
planner stage, it hands off to the part of the system that actually
takes actions.

**kristy liu:**
然后它会决定如何调查。在规划阶段之后，它会把任务交给系统中实际采取行动的部分。

**kristy liu:** This part runs the searches. Uses the tools and does the
heavy lifting to carry out the investigation. Now, depending on what
happens during the process.

**kristy liu:**
这部分负责运行搜索，使用工具并承担繁重的工作来执行调查。现在，根据过程中发生的情况。

**kristy liu:** We get one of the three possible outcomes. If the result
is unclear, or something doesn't look right, the system goes back to the
planner and to rethink the approach.

**kristy liu:**
我们会得到三种可能的结果之一。如果结果不清楚，或者有什么看起来不对劲，系统会回到规划器重新思考方法。

**kristy liu:** If everything looks good, it builds a reusable playbook.
If it's not a real threat, it marks it as a false positive.

**kristy liu:**
如果一切看起来都很好，它会构建一个可重复使用的剧本。如果不是真正的威胁，它会将其标记为误报。

**kristy liu:** This is how a gentle AI process works at a high level,
from planning to action to outcome.

**kristy liu:**
这就是智能AI流程在高层次上的工作方式，从规划到行动再到结果。

know, problems you didn't know existed. So we do encourage you to reach
out to the people that you're seeing today, um, not just to share
compliments, which are well-deserved, but also to ask.

**Marina Stojanovic:**
来解决一些非常简单或复杂，或者你甚至不知道存在的问题。所以我们确实鼓励你联系你今天看到的人，不仅仅是分享赞美，这些赞美是当之无愧的，也是为了提问。

**Marina Stojanovic:** Any questions, and stay curious and stay
connected about AI. Again, great job. Thank you, Caleb and Christy.

**Marina Stojanovic:**
任何问题，并对AI保持好奇和联系。再次，干得好。谢谢你，Caleb和Christy。

**kristy liu:** Thank you

**kristy liu:** 谢谢你。

**Marina Stojanovic:** 太棒了。我们确实有一些问题要问你，对吧，Keki？

### 用例7：Daisy Dool - AI赋能客户规划流程

**Daisy Dool:** Perfect. Thank you. Let me just share my screen.

**Daisy Dool:** 完美。谢谢你。我这就分享我的屏幕。

**Daisy Dool:** Fantastic. Thank you, everybody, for your patience, and
a warm hello from me.

**Daisy Dool:** 太棒了。谢谢大家的耐心等待，我向大家致以热烈的问候。

**Daisy Dool:** I am Daisy, and I'm an Enablement Program Manager. I
design and manage programs and empower customer-facing teams, like sales
and customer success, so they can do their best work. My focus is on
driving efficiency, boosting productivity, and creating learning
experiences that truly support our revenue goals.

**Daisy Dool:**
我是Daisy，一名赋能项目经理。我设计和管理项目，并赋能面向客户的团队，如销售和客户成功团队，让他们能做到最好。我的重点是提高效率、提升生产力，并创造真正支持我们收入目标的学习体验。

**Daisy Dool:** Whether that's increasing pipeline, improving customer
retention, or enabling teams to confidently navigate complex processes.

**Daisy Dool:**
无论是增加销售管道、提高客户保留率，还是让团队能够自信地应对复杂流程。

**Daisy Dool:** I work cross-functionally with sales, customer success,
professional services, product and marketing, to build scalable training
paths, launch new tools, and workflows, and ensure teams have what they
need at the right time.

**Daisy Dool:**
我与销售、客户成功、专业服务、产品和市场营销等部门跨职能合作，构建可扩展的培训路径，推出新工具和工作流程，并确保团队在正确的时间获得所需的支持。

**Daisy Dool:** To succeed with their customers. Today, I'm sharing how
we reimagined a core workflow using AI.

**Daisy Dool:**
与他们的客户一起成功。今天，我将分享我们如何使用AI重新构想一个核心工作流程。

**Daisy Dool:** Specifically. How we helped account executives reclaim
hours of planning time by using tools they already have.

**Daisy Dool:**
具体来说，我们如何通过使用他们已有的工具，帮助客户主管节省数小时的规划时间。

**Daisy Dool:** No new platforms, no steep learning curves, just a
smarter. More intentional approach.

**Daisy Dool:**
没有新平台，没有陡峭的学习曲线，只有一个更聪明、更有目的性的方法。

**Daisy Dool:** This year, we rolled out a new customer engagement model
for our enterprise customer-facing teams, like sales, CS, and PS.

**Daisy Dool:**
今年，我们为我们的企业客户服务团队，如销售、客户成功（CS）和专业服务（PS）团队，推出了一个新的客户互动模型。

**Daisy Dool:** The goal was to create greater consistency and alignment
in how we support our customers.

**Daisy Dool:** 目标是在我们支持客户的方式上创造更大的一致性和协调性。

**Daisy Dool:** Especially in more complex strategic accounts. With that
came the need for a more structured and visible way to collaborate
across teams. And that's where account planning came in.

**Daisy Dool:**
特别是在更复杂的战略客户中。随之而来的是对更结构化、更可视化的跨团队协作方式的需求。这就是客户规划的用武之地。

**Daisy Dool:** As a part of this new model, we introduced account
planning as a key motion for context and account plan is a shared
document that helps teams rely on customer goals.

**Daisy Dool:**
作为这个新模型的一部分，我们引入了客户规划作为关键的背景动作，而客户计划是一个共享文档，帮助团队依赖客户目标。

**Daisy Dool:** Identify risks and blockers, map out key stakeholders,
and document how we plan to engage and grow the account strategically.

**Daisy Dool:**
识别风险和障碍，规划关键利益相关者，并记录我们计划如何战略性地与客户互动并发展客户。

**Daisy Dool:** But very quickly, we realized that creating these
account plans, while important, was also really time-consuming. Account
executives told us it was taking 3-5 hours, and most of that time was
spent summarizing what they already knew, not building strategy.

**Daisy Dool:**
但很快，我们意识到创建这些客户计划虽然重要，但也非常耗时。客户主管告诉我们这需要3-5个小时，而大部分时间都花在了总结他们已经知道的事情上，而不是制定策略。

**Daisy Dool:** So we had a critical motion that was meant to support
deeper engagement strategy, but it wasn't scaling.

**Daisy Dool:**
所以我们有一个旨在支持更深层次互动策略的关键举措，但它没有扩展。

**Daisy Dool:** That was the challenge we needed to solve. We didn't
want to throw out the process, we just needed to modernize how we
supported it. That's what led us to rethink the workflow using AI.

**Daisy Dool:**
这就是我们需要解决的挑战。我们不想抛弃这个流程，我们只是需要现代化我们支持它的方式。这就是促使我们使用AI重新思考工作流程的原因。

**Daisy Dool:** We didn't bring in any new tools, we just leaned into
what we already had access to.

**Daisy Dool:**
我们没有引入任何新工具，我们只是利用了我们已经拥有的资源。

**Daisy Dool:** For those who may not be familiar, Gong is our
conversational intelligence platform. It captures and transcribes
customer calls, and then uses AI to surface trends, like what topics are
being discussed, how many… how much a customer is speaking, and even
indicators of risk or momentum.

**Daisy Dool:**
对于那些可能不熟悉的人来说，Gong是我们的对话智能平台。它捕捉和转录客户通话，然后使用AI来发现趋势，比如正在讨论什么话题，客户说了多少话，甚至风险或势头的指标。

**Daisy Dool:** Quip is our collaborative workspace. It's where account
executives and other members of customer-facing teams document the
account plans. It's live, edible, and in context.

**Daisy Dool:**
Quip是我们的协作工作空间。客户主管和面向客户团队的其他成员在这里记录客户计划。它是实时的、可编辑的，并且与上下文相关。

**Daisy Dool:** It also integrates directly with Salesforce, so it
becomes a part of the workflow, not an extra step.

**Daisy Dool:**
它还直接与Salesforce集成，因此它成为工作流程的一部分，而不是一个额外的步骤。

**Daisy Dool:** What we did was introduce a workflow that connects the
two.

**Daisy Dool:** 我们所做的是引入一个连接这两者的工作流程。

**Daisy Dool:** Gong gives us the insights, and Copilot helps structure
those into a draft account plan that's ready for QUIP.

**Daisy Dool:**
Gong为我们提供洞察，而Copilot帮助将这些洞察构建成一个准备好用于QUIP的客户计划草案。

**Daisy Dool:** The goal here wasn't to automate thinking, it was to
save reps time on summarizing and formatting so they could focus on
strategy, and importantly, every plan still goes through a human filter.

**Daisy Dool:**
这里的目标不是自动化思考，而是为代表节省总结和格式化的时间，让他们能专注于策略，而且重要的是，每个计划仍然经过人工筛选。

**Daisy Dool:** Reps tweak, adjust, and make it their own. It's still
their voice, just with a head start.

**Daisy Dool:**
代表们会调整、修改，并使其成为自己的东西。这仍然是他们的声音，只是有了一个领先的开端。

**Daisy Dool:** Before I show you the work… how the workflow works, I
want to quickly highlight what we were able to unlock by rethinking our
approach.

**Daisy Dool:**
在我向你展示工作流程如何运作之前，我想快速强调一下我们通过重新思考方法所能解锁的东西。

**Daisy Dool:** First, we took what used to be a 3-5 hour task building
an account plan, and turned it into something reps could kick off in
about 15 minutes.

**Daisy Dool:**
首先，我们将过去需要3-5小时才能完成的客户计划制定任务，变成了一个代表们可以在大约15分钟内启动的事情。

**Daisy Dool:** That shift gave them back time to focus on strategy, not
documentation.

**Daisy Dool:** 这种转变让他们有时间专注于策略，而不是文档工作。

**Daisy Dool:** They could spend more time thinking about what moves the
account for, not just capturing what already happened.

**Daisy Dool:**
他们可以花更多时间思考如何推动客户发展，而不仅仅是记录已经发生的事情。

**Daisy Dool:** We also introduced a repeatable playbook that meant
teams weren't starting from scratch, and leaders could more easily coach
to a consistent process.

**Daisy Dool:**
我们还引入了一个可重复的剧本，这意味着团队不必从零开始，领导者可以更容易地指导一个一致的流程。

**Daisy Dool:** And along the way, we improved our data hygiene. As we
rolled this out, we uncovered issues with contact records.

**Daisy Dool:**
在此过程中，我们改善了我们的数据卫生。在推出这个过程中，我们发现了联系人记录的问题。

**Daisy Dool:** And CRM alignment that we wouldn't have noticed
otherwise. It helped us clean up the foundation we were building
insights on.

**Daisy Dool:**

**Daisy Dool:** And lastly, this approach is scalable. What we built for

**Daisy Dool:**

### 用例8：Jenna Paglia - AI驱动的客户利用率分析

**Jenna Paglia:** Yes, I am here, and I am ready to go.

**Jenna Paglia:** 是的，我在这里，我准备好了。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Amazing. Over to you, Jenna.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 太棒了。交给你了，Jenna。

**Jenna Paglia:** Can you just give me a thumbs up that you can see my
screen?

**Jenna Paglia:** 你能给我一个赞，确认你能看到我的屏幕吗？

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Yes, we can.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 是的，我们可以。

**Jenna Paglia:** Okay, and let me make sure I'm sharing with sound.
Okay, perfect. I'm ready to go.

**Jenna Paglia:** 好的，让我确保我分享了声音。好的，完美。我准备好了。

**Jenna Paglia:** Hi, everyone! My name is Jenna Paglia. I am the Sales
Enablement Manager on the Revenue Enablement Team, and I am so excited
to be talking about our AI use case today. My project was in conjunction
with solution architect Jeff Wright. He's not on with me today, but he
recorded a fabulous demo, which we will see in a bit.

**Jenna Paglia:** 大家好！我叫Jenna
Paglia。我是收入赋能团队的销售赋能经理，我非常兴奋今天能谈论我们的AI用例。我的项目是与解决方案架构师Jeff
Wright合作的。他今天不在，但他录制了一个精彩的演示，我们稍后会看到。

**Jenna Paglia:** Our use of AI will empower the go-to-market teams to
easily understand customer utilization data and have more meaningful
conversations with customers about business outcomes.

**Jenna Paglia:**
我们对AI的使用将赋能市场推广团队，让他们能轻松理解客户使用数据，并与客户就业务成果进行更有意义的对话。

**Jenna Paglia:** About business outcomes. A lot of prep went into this.
For example, I went as far to watch Back to the Future for the first
time last weekend, so I've never felt more ready to talk about advancing
technology.

**Jenna Paglia:**
关于业务成果。这方面做了很多准备。例如，我上周末第一次看了《回到未来》，所以我从未感觉比现在更准备好谈论先进技术了。

**Jenna Paglia:** I wanted to start by talking a little bit about the
problem we were facing.

**Jenna Paglia:** 我想从我们面临的问题开始谈起。

**Jenna Paglia:** 360 Insights is an incredibly powerful tool which
provides us with an abundance of data, including customer product
utilization and performance metrics.

**Jenna Paglia:** 360
Insights是一个非常强大的工具，它为我们提供了大量数据，包括客户产品使用率和性能指标。

**Jenna Paglia:** However, with this increase in data availability, the
senior care sales and customer success teams were faced with a
double-edged sword.

**Jenna Paglia:**
然而，随着数据可用性的增加，老年护理销售和客户成功团队面临着一把双刃剑。

**Jenna Paglia:** A great amount of information to interpret… oh, sorry,
a great amount of information, but also a great amount of information to
interpret.

**Jenna Paglia:**
大量的信息需要解读……哦，抱歉，是大量的信息，但也是大量需要解读的信息。

**Jenna Paglia:** Reps can spend up to an hour interpreting utilization
and performance data for a single customer call.

**Jenna Paglia:**
代表们可能需要花费长达一个小时来解读单个客户通话的使用率和性能数据。

**Jenna Paglia:** Now, in revenue enablement, our job is to support the
go-to-market teams, and their problems are our problems.

**Jenna Paglia:**
现在，在收入赋能方面，我们的工作是支持市场推广团队，他们的问题就是我们的问题。

**Jenna Paglia:** We wanted to come up with a way to enable our teams to
really easily understand the data in 360 Insights.

**Jenna Paglia:** 我们想找到一种方法，让我们的团队能够真正轻松地理解360
Insights中的数据。

**Jenna Paglia:** Cut down on the amount of time spent interpreting that
data, and ultimately, give them that time back to focus on what really
matters.

**Jenna Paglia:**
减少解读数据所花费的时间，并最终将这些时间还给他们，让他们专注于真正重要的事情。

**Jenna Paglia:** How can we help our customers deliver exceptional
care? Enter AI, our solution.

**Jenna Paglia:**
我们如何能帮助我们的客户提供卓越的护理？答案是AI，我们的解决方案。

**Jenna Paglia:** We created an army of AI agents that can do all of the
heavy lifting for our reps when it comes to interpreting data for
specific point-click care products.

**Jenna Paglia:**
我们创建了一支AI智能体大军，它们可以为我们的代表们承担所有繁重的数据解读工作，特别是针对特定的PointClickCare产品。

**Jenna Paglia:** These AI agents translate raw utilization data from

business outcomes.

**Jenna Paglia:** 这些AI智能体将来自360
Insights的原始使用数据转化为趋势，然后这些趋势可以与客户的业务成果联系起来。

**Jenna Paglia:** I'm gonna hand things over to my partner on this

**Jenna Paglia:** 我要把话筒交给我在这个项目中的搭档Jeff

**Jenna Paglia:** Say that 5 times fast. Hopefully the sound is gonna
work on this.

**Jenna Paglia:** 快速说五遍。希望这个声音能起作用。

**Jenna Paglia:** We've been working on a tool to help. Show the
correlation between great outcomes.

**Jenna Paglia:** 我们一直在开发一个工具来帮助展示良好结果与……

**Jenna Paglia:** And adoption and utilization of our products. The

**Jenna Paglia:**

**Jenna Paglia:** Really simply, how we built it is to test to see if

**Jenna Paglia:** 很简单，我们构建它的方式是测试应用程序是否能工作。

**Jenna Paglia:**

**Jenna Paglia:** So there's a couple steps I'm going to show you here

**Jenna Paglia:**
所以我在这里要向你展示几个步骤，我们最终也希望将它们自动化。但首先我想向你展示的是，我们将获取一个客户的。

**Jenna Paglia:** Utilization data. So I'm using a customer's data, but
I've. Cleaned it up and making sure that we just use a fake name here.

**Jenna Paglia:**
使用数据。我正在使用一个客户的数据，但我已经清理过，并确保我们在这里只使用一个假名。

**Jenna Paglia:** Carecorp. So I'm going to upload CareCorp's. Infection
prevention and control, utilization data, and what I've asked it to do

**Jenna Paglia:**
Carecorp。所以我要上传CareCorp的感染预防与控制使用数据，我要求它做的是分组。

**Jenna Paglia:** The homes together in green, yellow, and red. Green

**Jenna Paglia:**
将这些家庭分为绿色、黄色和红色。绿色表示使用率高，黄色表示中等，红色表示。

**Jenna Paglia:** Utilize… it needs some work. And so what we've asked

**Jenna Paglia:**
使用……它需要一些工作。所以我们要求它做的是将那些家庭分组，这样我们就能看到，这些使用组之间是否存在相关性。

**Jenna Paglia:** And the outcomes that are related. Or should be
impacted by the use of this tool.

**Jenna Paglia:** 以及相关的结果，或者说应该受到这个工具使用影响的结果。

**Jenna Paglia:** So you can see here, down below, we have 18 homes that
are in that green zone.

**Jenna Paglia:** 所以你可以在下面看到，我们有18个家庭处于绿色区域。

**Jenna Paglia:** 14 in yellow, and 13 in red. The next steps, we
created a prompt that would then allow us to upload.

**Jenna Paglia:**
14个在黄色区域，13个在红色区域。下一步，我们创建了一个提示，允许我们上传。

**Jenna Paglia:** Outcome data. For the… for the actual agent to go in
and see if there's a correlation between the two. So I'm going to op…
I'm going to upload CareCorp's outcome.

**Jenna Paglia:**
结果数据。让实际的智能体介入，看看两者之间是否存在相关性。所以我要……我要上传CareCorp的结果。

**Jenna Paglia:** And in a few seconds, it'll add to that table and show

**Jenna Paglia:** 几秒钟后，它会添加到那个表格中并向我们展示。

**Jenna Paglia:** The green group, the yellow group, and the red groups.
Outcome data related to infections.

**Jenna Paglia:** 绿色组、黄色组和红色组。与感染相关的结果数据。

**Jenna Paglia:** So, as you can see here, very quickly, our green
group.

**Jenna Paglia:** 所以，正如你在这里看到的，很快，我们的绿色小组。

**Jenna Paglia:** Has the best outcomes with regards to percentage of

**Jenna Paglia:** 在长期居住居民尿路感染百分比方面取得了最佳结果。

**Jenna Paglia:** And average percent of infections where patients go

**Jenna Paglia:** 以及患者因感染返回医院的平均百分比。

**Jenna Paglia:** And you can see that in this case here, this example,

**Jenna Paglia:**

**Jenna Paglia:** We're hoping to apply this to, obviously, more

**Jenna Paglia:**
我们希望将此应用于更多的产品，而不仅仅是感染控制，并能够向我们的客户讲述这个伟大的故事。

**Jenna Paglia:** Thanks, Jeff. Great demo. So, to kind of go into a
little bit more context as to what we're seeing, to summarize.

**Jenna Paglia:**
谢谢，Jeff。很棒的演示。那么，为了更深入地了解我们所看到的情况，总结一下。

**Jenna Paglia:** Um, the AI agent that we created was to… able to
establish the facilities belonging to CareCorp into three categories.

**Jenna Paglia:** 我们创建的AI智能体能够将属于CareCorp的设施分为三类。

**Jenna Paglia:** Red for not-so-great utilization of our PCC products,
or sorry, IPC product.

**Jenna Paglia:** 红色代表我们PCC产品或IPC产品的使用率不佳。

**Jenna Paglia:** Yellow for moderate utilization, and green for optimal
utilization. It was then able to identify trends, and what it saw was
that facilities in the green zone, those with optimal utilization of our
IPC products, are showing the best results.

**Jenna Paglia:**
黄色代表中等使用率，绿色代表最佳使用率。然后它能够识别趋势，它看到的是，绿色区域的设施，也就是那些最佳使用我们IPC产品的设施，显示出最好的结果。

**Jenna Paglia:** They have fewer long-stay residents with urinary tract
infections and lower percentages of patients returning to the hospital
due to infections.

**Jenna Paglia:**
他们的长期居住居民尿路感染较少，因感染返回医院的患者百分比较低。

**Jenna Paglia:** Great. So this demonstrates a correlation between the
adoption and effective utilization of our solution and the improved
performance of these facilities.

**Jenna Paglia:**
太棒了。所以这证明了我们解决方案的采用和有效利用与这些设施性能改善之间的相关性。

**Jenna Paglia:** So, it's important to note that we're using AI for
correlation, not causation.

**Jenna Paglia:**
所以，需要注意的是，我们使用AI是为了寻找相关性，而不是因果关系。

**Jenna Paglia:** While we have this information, it's great, but we
can't directly tell our customers, if you use IPC, you'll see a
reduction in rehospitalizations.

**Jenna Paglia:**
虽然我们有这些信息，这很棒，但我们不能直接告诉我们的客户，如果你使用IPC，你会看到再入院率的降低。

**Jenna Paglia:** But what we can do is show them the trends within
their own facilities that support these better business outcomes.

**Jenna Paglia:**
但我们能做的是向他们展示他们自己设施内的趋势，这些趋势支持了更好的业务成果。

**Jenna Paglia:** And allow them to connect those dots back to our
utilization of our point-click care products.

**Jenna Paglia:**
并让他们将这些点与我们PointClickCare产品的使用联系起来。

**Jenna Paglia:** It's also important to mention that these AI agents
aren't meant to replace the work our reps do, but rather empower them to
have more meaningful conversations about product utilization and the
impact on business outcomes with our customers.

**Jenna Paglia:**
同样重要的是要提到，这些AI智能体并非旨在取代我们代表的工作，而是赋能他们与客户就产品使用及其对业务成果的影响进行更有意义的对话。

**Jenna Paglia:** Now, if you're in sales or customer success, I know
what your question's gonna be, uh, when the heck do I get to try this?

**Jenna Paglia:**
现在，如果你在销售或客户成功部门，我知道你的问题会是什么，我到底什么时候能试试这个？

**Jenna Paglia:** And to that, I say stay tuned. We will be sharing more

**Jenna Paglia:** 对此，我说敬请期待。我们将在未来几周分享更多细节。

**Jenna Paglia:**
这就是我今天为大家准备的全部内容。我非常感谢你们的时间。我将开放提问环节。

**Marina Stojanovic:** Thank you so much, Jenna! We have a lot of

### 主持人互动：对AI的礼貌

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Um, so now, it's time for some real talk. While we
wait, let's talk about who here says please and thank you to their AI
assistants.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
那么，现在是时候说点实在的了。在我们等待的时候，我们来谈谈这里有谁会对他们的AI助手说“请”和“谢谢”。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** How about you, Marina? Do you say please and thank
you when you interact with AI?

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 你呢，Marina？你在与AI互动时会说“请”和“谢谢”吗？

**Marina Stojanovic:** I do. However, Alexa's the only exception,
because she likes to sass me.

**Marina Stojanovic:**
我会。不过，Alexa是唯一的例外，因为她喜欢对我无礼。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Okay.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 好的。

**Marina Stojanovic:** And she doesn't really do what I want her to do,
so I don't… I actually argue with her.

**Marina Stojanovic:**
而且她并不真正做我想让她做的事，所以我不会……我实际上会和她争论。

**Marina Stojanovic:** Um, but the… if I am typing it into the… into the
screen, and it can be traced back to me, I absolutely do, because if
they ever become self-aware, I want to be spared. What can I say?

**Marina Stojanovic:**
但是……如果我把它输入到屏幕上，并且可以追溯到我，我绝对会这么做，因为如果它们有一天变得有自我意识，我希望被幸免。我能说什么呢？

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Yeah, absolutely, I agree with you. I want to be on
their nice list as well.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
是的，当然，我同意你的看法。我也想在他们的好人名单上。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** But here's something I've been reading about.
Technically, no, we don't have to be polite to, you know, any AI agent
or any AI assistant. Ai doesn't have feelings, no consciousness, or….

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
但这是我最近读到的一些东西。从技术上讲，不，我们不必对任何AI智能体或AI助手有礼貌。AI没有感情，没有意识，或者……

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Social expectations. So it doesn't really get
offended or even feel appreciated if you keep saying please and thank
you.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
社会期望。所以如果你一直说“请”和“谢谢”，它并不会真的被冒犯，甚至不会感到被欣赏。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** However, socially and psychologically, yes, it can
be a good idea to be polite to AI, and here's why.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
然而，从社会和心理角度来看，是的，对AI有礼貌可能是一个好主意，原因如下。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** It reinforces empathy, not for AI, but it actually
does reinforce empathy and kindness for the person talking to AI.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
它增强了同理心，不是对AI，而是实际上增强了与AI交谈的人的同理心和善良。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** And more importantly, it models good behavior. And,
you know, even good language for AI.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
更重要的是，它树立了良好的行为榜样。而且，你知道，甚至为AI树立了良好的语言榜样。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** As AI continues to become more human-like in
conversations, polite language might actually help, and it might
influence how AI is being trained to respond.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
随着AI在对话中变得越来越像人类，礼貌的语言实际上可能会有所帮助，并且可能会影响AI被训练如何回应。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** So, let's take a look at what our audience thinks.
Anything from the audience?

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
那么，让我们看看我们的观众是怎么想的。观众有什么看法吗？

**Marina Stojanovic:** A lot of yeses, a lot of yeses. Uh, I heard
threatening gives you the best results, but I'm not taking my chance.
Good move, Jennifer! I appreciate that.

**Marina Stojanovic:**
很多“是”，很多“是”。我听说威胁能得到最好的结果，但我不想冒险。干得好，Jennifer！我很欣赏。

**Marina Stojanovic:** Um, we have Melissa Jackson. I say please before
prompt, but I've never said thank you. Uh-oh. It's gonna remember that,
Melissa, just wait. Um, if they become self-aware, it's over for Jeff.

**Marina Stojanovic:** 我们有Melissa
Jackson。我在提示前会说“请”，但我从没说过“谢谢”。哦哦。它会记住的，Melissa，等着瞧。如果它们变得有自我意识，Jeff就完蛋了。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Very interesting.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 非常有趣。

**Marina Stojanovic:** Sorry, for Jonathan, he read an article that
threatening your AI Makes the Prompt Better. My prompts are real good.

**Marina Stojanovic:**
抱歉，对于Jonathan，他读了一篇文章说威胁你的AI能让提示变得更好。我的提示真的很好。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Oh my god. Wow. But here's an interesting angle. I
don't know if anyone read about this. There is a cost to being polite to
AI. Has anyone read about that article that came out very recently from
OpenAI? So, you know, just using phrases like, please, thank you.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
天哪。哇。但这里有一个有趣的角度。我不知道有没有人读过这个。对AI有礼貌是有代价的。有人读过OpenAI最近发表的那篇文章吗？所以，你知道，只是使用像“请”、“谢谢”这样的短语。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** They actually do increase the number of tokens in a
prompt, so the number of words increase, therefore it's a very marginal
increase. Technically.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
它们实际上会增加提示中的令牌（token：AI模型处理文本的基本单位）数量，所以词语数量增加，因此这是一个非常微小的增加。从技术上讲。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** It's a very small cost, but it does increase the
cost.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 这是一个非常小的成本，但它确实增加了成本。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Um, so there's no official research proving it, but
there is some anecdotal data, and I've even heard this in some of the
trainings done by Microsoft, that.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
所以没有官方研究证明这一点，但有一些轶事数据，我甚至在微软的一些培训中听说过。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** There is actually, you know, some influence on the
model's tone. It doesn't mean if you are nice to the model, it'll give
you good responses, otherwise it won't, that's totally not true.
However, if you… it tries to mimic your tone. So, if you are more
thoughtful, and if you are more polite while asking questions, it might
mimic the same tone, and it might lead to better, more thoughtful, or
even more nuanced results.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
实际上，对模型的语气有一些影响。这并不意味着如果你对模型友好，它就会给你好的回应，否则就不会，那完全不是真的。然而，如果你……它会尝试模仿你的语气。所以，如果你在提问时更周到、更有礼貌，它可能会模仿同样的语气，并可能带来更好、更周到，甚至更细致的结果。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** So, does anyone here have any experiences with
that? Um, while I know politeness doesn't really change the factual
accuracy of the data or the results that you get, do you find a subtle
change in maybe the tone or the depth of your argument or your
engagement with AI? Tell us in the chat.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
那么，这里有人有这方面的经验吗？虽然我知道礼貌并不会真正改变数据的真实性或你得到的结果，但你是否发现与AI的互动中，语气或论点深度有细微的变化？在聊天中告诉我们。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** What do you think? Especially when you're trying to
generate something very creative.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
你怎么看？特别是当你试图生成一些非常有创意的东西时。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Or when you're getting AI, maybe the writing coach.
Writing coach is a great example, because it can actually create.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
或者当你使用AI，比如写作教练时。写作教练是一个很好的例子，因为它实际上可以创造。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Poetry for you, it can create essays for you. So
what does that look like? Have you noticed a change?

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
为你写诗，为你写文章。那是什么样子的？你注意到变化了吗？

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Tell us in the chat. Let's see what everyone's
saying.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 在聊天中告诉我们。让我们看看大家都在说什么。

**Marina Stojanovic:** Be Canadian. I love it. Keep the responses
coming, we'll keep reading them as we go along.

**Marina Stojanovic:**
做个加拿大人。我喜欢。请继续回应，我们会边走边读。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Be canoe! I love that.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 做个独木舟！我喜欢那个。

**Marina Stojanovic:** Um, going down the wrong path, stop generating,
and right. Oh, that's all I have to say. All I have to say is she… Alexa
started it, so let's, uh, you know, that's not my fault. She's… she's
like this.

**Marina Stojanovic:**
走错了路，停止生成，对。哦，这就是我要说的。我只想说，是她……是Alexa先开始的，所以，你知道，那不是我的错。她……她就是这样。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Oh my god, okay, so next up….

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 天哪，好的，那么接下来……

**Ketki Yennemadi:** That's amazing. Next up, we have a very interesting
and insightful use case by Litza from OCIO.

**Ketki Yennemadi:**
太棒了。接下来，我们有一个来自OCIO（首席信息官办公室）的Litza带来的非常有趣且富有洞察力的用例。

**Marina Stojanovic:** Alright.

**Marina Stojanovic:** 好的。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Um, on an AI agent called Profit. I'm very curious.

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 关于一个叫做Profit的AI智能体。我很好奇。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 请讲，Lipta。

### 用例9：Lipsa Mishra - Copado AI在软件开发生命周期中的应用

**Lipsa Mishra:** Please let me know when you are able to see my screen.

**Lipsa Mishra:** 当你能看到我的屏幕时，请告诉我。

**Ketki Yennemadi:** Yes, we can see it now

**Ketki Yennemadi:** 是的，我们现在能看到了。

**Lipsa Mishra:** Thank you. So my AI tool is Capato AI. And it's going

introduce myself first. This is Lipsa.

**Lipsa Mishra:** 谢谢你。我的AI工具是Copado
AI。它将……它将向我展示，不，嘿，我先自我介绍一下。我是Lipsa。

**Lipsa Mishra:** Uh, I'm the senior manager from OSAO. The AI tool is
Capado AI, and I'm trying to showcase that.

**Lipsa Mishra:**

AI，我正试图展示它。

**Lipsa Mishra:** Uh, how using Capato AI, we can streamline our
software development lifecycle.

**Lipsa Mishra:** 如何使用Copado AI来简化我们的软件开发生命周期。

**Lipsa Mishra:** From requirement intake through our development. So,
bear with me a little bit.

**Lipsa Mishra:** 从需求接收到我们的开发。所以，请耐心听我讲一下。

**Marina Stojanovic:** Yep, so can we get you to do it in presenter

**Marina Stojanovic:**
